Task instruction sent to agent 
# Fix Work Search Query Processing for Edge-Case Inputs

**Repository:** internetarchive/openlibrary
**Language:** Python
**Difficulty:** hard

## Problem

Following the introduction of the `SearchScheme`-based work search, raw user queries are not consistently normalized and escaped before reaching Solr. Inputs with trailing dashes, reserved operators, or quoted strings can be misinterpreted by the parser under the current work search scheme, leading to parse errors or unintended queries.

## Reproduction

1. Open the work search page, enter a query ending with a hyphen (e.g., `Horror-`), and submit
2. Observe that the request fails or does not yield results due to query parsing issues
3. Similar issues occur with inputs containing operator-like tokens or quoted phrases

## Key Components

- `WorkSearchScheme.process_user_query` — the entry point where raw user input is processed for Solr
- Solr query construction and escaping logic in the worksearch plugin

## Task

1. Locate `WorkSearchScheme.process_user_query` and trace how raw user input flows to Solr
2. Fix normalization and escaping to handle: trailing dashes, operator-like tokens, quoted phrases, and ISBN-like strings
3. Ensure the fix produces safely escaped, semantically correct Solr queries for all edge cases
4. Verify that standard (non-edge-case) searches are unaffected
5. Run existing tests to ensure no regressions

## Success Criteria

- Queries with trailing hyphens (e.g., `Horror-`) execute without Solr errors
- Operator-like tokens and quoted phrases are properly escaped
- ISBN-like strings are handled correctly
- Standard search queries continue to work as expected
- All existing tests pass

    20→    universe: frozenset[str]
    21→    # All actual solr fields that can be in a user query
    22→    all_fields: frozenset[str]
    23→    # Fields that can be read, but which aren't stored in solr

    38→    def __init__(self, lang: str | None = None):

     6→from luqum.tree import BaseOperation, Group, Item, SearchField, Unary, Word
     7→
     8→
     9→class EmptyTreeError(Exception):
    10→    pass
    11→
    12→
    13→def luqum_remove_child(child: Item, parents: list[Item]):
    14→    """
    15→    Removes a child from a luqum parse tree. If the tree
    16→    ends up being empty, errors.
    17→
    18→    :param child: Node to remove
    19→    :param parents: Path of parent nodes leading from the root of the tree
    20→    """
    21→    parent = parents[-1] if parents else None
    22→    if parent is None:
    23→        # We cannot remove the element if it is the root of the tree
    24→        raise EmptyTreeError
    25→    elif isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):
    26→        new_children = tuple(c for c in parent.children if c != child)
    27→        if not new_children:
    28→            # If we have deleted all the children, we need to delete the parent
    29→            # as well. And potentially recurse up the tree.
    30→            luqum_remove_child(parent, parents[:-1])
    31→        else:
    32→            parent.children = new_children
    33→    else:
    34→        raise NotImplementedError(
    35→            f"Not implemented for Item subclass: {parent.__class__.__name__}"
    36→        )
    37→
    38→
    39→def luqum_replace_child(parent: Item, old_child: Item, new_child: Item):
    40→    """
    41→    Replaces a child in a luqum parse tree.
    42→    """
    43→    if isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):
    44→        new_children = tuple(
    45→            new_child if c == old_child else c for

     8→
     9→class EmptyTreeError(Exception):
    10→    pass
    11→
    12→
    13→def luqum_remove_child(child: Item, parents: list[Item]):
    14→    """
    15→    Removes a child from a luqum parse tree. If the tree
    16→    ends up being empty, errors.
    17→
    18→    :param child: Node to remove
    19→    :param parents: Path of parent nodes leading from the root of the tree
    20→    """
    21→    parent = parents[-1] if parents else None
    22→    if parent is None:
    23→        # We cannot remove the element if it is the root of the tree
    24→        raise EmptyTreeError
    25→    elif isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):
    26→        new_children = tuple(c for c in parent.children if c != child)
    27→        if not new_children:
    28→            # If we have deleted all the children, we need to delete the parent
    29→            # as well. And potentially recurse up the tree.
    30→            luqum_remove_child(parent, parents[:-1])
    31→        else:
    32→            parent.children = new_children
    33→    else:
    34→        raise NotImplementedError(
    35→            f"Not implemented for Item subclass: {parent.__class__.__name__}"
    36→        )
    37→
    38→
    39→def luqum_replace_child(parent: Item, old_child: Item, new_child: Item):
    40→    """
    41→    Replaces a child in a luqum parse tree.
    42→    """
    43→    if isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):
    44→        new_children = tuple(
    45→            new_child if c == old_child else c for
... (truncated)

77-usertool_resultBash
def escape_unknown_fields(
    query: str,
    is_valid_field: Callable[[str], bool],
    lower=True,
) -> str:
    """
    Escapes the colon of any search field that is not deemed valid by the
    predicate function `is_valid_field`.

    :param query: Query to escape
    :param is_valid_field: Predicate function that determines if a field is valid
    :param lower: If true, the field will be lowercased before being checked

    >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo', lambda field: False)
    'title\\\\:foo'
    >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo bar   blah:bar baz:boo', lambda field: False)
    'title\\\\:foo bar   blah\\\\:bar baz\\\\:boo'
    >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo bar', {'title'}.__contains__)
    'title:foo bar'
    >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo bar baz:boo', {'title'}.__contains__)
    'title:foo bar baz\\\\:boo'

    87→    def process_user_query(self, q_param: str) -> str:
    88→        if q_param == '*:*':
    89→            # This is a special solr syntax; don't process
    90→            return q_param
    91→
    92→        try:
    93→            q_param = escape_unknown_fields(
    94→                (
    95→                    # Solr 4+ has support for regexes (eg `key:/foo.*/`)! But for now,
    96→                    # let's not expose that and escape all '/'. Otherwise
    97→                    # `key:/works/OL1W` is interpreted as a regex.
    98→                    q_param.strip()
    99→                    .replace('/', '\\/')
   100→                    # Also escape unexposed lucene features
   101→                    .replace('?', '\\?')
   102→                    .replace('~', '\\~')
   103→                ),
   104→                self.is_search_field,
   105→                lower=True,
   106→            )
   107→            q_tree = luqum_parser(q_param)
   108→        except ParseError:
   109→            # This isn't a syntactically valid lucene query
   110→            logger.warning("Invalid lucene query", exc_info=True)
   111→            # Escape everything we can
   112→            q_tree = luqum_parser(fully_escape_query(q_param))
   113→
   114→        q_tree = self.transform_user_query(q_param, q_tree)
   115→        return str(q_tree)
   116→

## Summary of Exploration: OpenLibrary WorkSearch Plugin Structure

I've thoroughly explored the worksearch plugin structure and identified the test expectations, implementation flow, and where fixes are needed. Here's what I found:

### 1. Test Files and Test Patterns

**Test File Location:** `/workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/plugins/worksearch/schemes/tests/test_works.py`

**Test Data Structure (QUERY_PARSER_TESTS):** A dictionary with 23+ test cases validating `process_user_query` behavior:

**Key test cases:**
- **"Invalid dashes"**: `"foo foo bar -"` → `"foo foo bar \\-"` (escape trailing dash)
- **"Unmatched double-quote"**: `'title:Compilation Group for the "History of Modern China'` → `'title\\:Compilation Group for the \\"History of Modern China'`
- **"Colons in query"**: `"flatland:a romance of many dimensions"` → `"flatland\\:a romance of many dimensions"`
- **"Spaced colons in query"**: `"flatland : a romance of many dimensions"` → `"flatland\\: a romance of many dimensions"`
- **"ISBN-like"**: `"978-0-06-093546-7"` → `"isbn:(9780060935467)"` (auto-detect and normalize)
- **Field aliases**: Map user field names (author, by, title) to solr field names (author_name, alternative_title)
- **Operators**: Preserve OR/AND operators while transforming fields

**Expected behavior patterns:**
1. Unknown fields (colons without valid field names) should be escaped: `fieldname:` → `fieldname\\:`
2. Special characters like `-`, `"`, `~`, `/`, `?` should be escaped when not used as operators
3. Valid field names should be mapped and their values grouped: `author:pollan` → `author_name:pollan`
4. ISBN-like patterns should be auto-detected and normalized
5. Unmatched quotes should be escaped entirely

    19→class SearchScheme:
    20→    # Set of queries that define the universe of this scheme
    21→    universe: frozenset[str]
    22→    # All actual solr fields that can be in a user query
    23→    all_fields: frozenset[str]
    24→    # Fields that can be read, but which aren't stored in solr
    25→    non_solr_fields: frozenset[str]
    26→    # These fields are fetched for facets and can also be url params
    27→    facet_fields: frozenset[str]
    28→    # Mapping of user-only fields to solr fields
    29→    field_name_map: MappingProxyType[str, str]
    30→    # Mapping of user sort to solr sort
    31→    sorts: MappingProxyType[str, str | Callable[[], str]]
    32→    # Default
    33→    default_fetched_fields: frozenset[str]
    34→    # Fields that should be rewritten
    35→    facet_rewrites: MappingProxyType[tuple[str, str], str | Callable[[], str]]
    36→    # Language of user
    37→    lang: str
    38→
    39→    def __init__(self, lang: str | None = None):
    40→        # Fall back to web.ctx.lang until we move away from it
    41→        self.lang = lang or getattr(web.ctx, 'lang', None) or 'en'
    42→
    43→    def is_search_field(self, field: str):
    44→        return field in self.all_fields or field in self.field_name_map

    88→    def process_user_query(self, q_param: str) -> str:
    89→        if q_param == '*:*':
    90→            # This is a special solr syntax; don't process
    91→            return q_param
    92→
    93→        try:
    94→            # Pre-escape the query to handle edge cases before parsing
    95→            sanitized_query = (
    96→                # Solr 4+ has support for regexes (eg `key:/foo.*/`)! But for now,
    97→                # let's not expose that and escape all '/'. Otherwise
    98→                # `key:/works/OL1W` is interpreted as a regex.
    99→                q_param.strip()
   100→                .replace('/', '\\/')
   101→                # Also escape unexposed lucene features
   102→                .replace('?', '\\?')
   103→                .replace('~', '\\~')
   104→            )
   105→
   106→            # Escape trailing and isolated operators (- or +) that would cause parse errors
   107→            # These patterns handle:
   108→            # - Trailing dash/plus at end of string
   109→            # - Dash/plus surrounded by spaces (isolated)
   110→            # - Dash/plus at start of string followed by space
   111→            # - Dash/plus after opening paren followed by space/end
   112→            # - While preserving dashes in ISBNs and compound words like "foo-bar"
   113→            sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])(-|\+)\s*$', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
   114→            sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', sanitized_query)
   115→            sanitized_query = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
   116→            sanitized_query = re.sub(
   117→                r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)', r'(\\\1', sanitized_query
   118→            )

   124→def fully_escape_query(query: str) -> str:
   125→    """
   126→    Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string.
   127→
   128→    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')
   129→    'title\\\\:foo'
   130→    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')
   131→    'title\\\\:foo bar'
   132→    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo (bar baz:boo)')
   133→    'title\\\\:foo \\\\(bar baz\\\\:boo\\\\)'
   134→    >>> fully_escape_query('x:[A TO Z}')
   135→    'x\\\\:\\\\[A TO Z\\\\}'
   136→    >>> fully_escape_query('foo AND bar')
   137→    'foo and bar'
   138→    >>> fully_escape_query("foo's bar")
   139→    "foo\\\\'s bar"
   140→    """
   141→    escaped = query
   142→    # Escape special characters
   143→    escaped = re.sub(r'[\[\]\(\)\{\}:"\-+?~^/\\,\']', r'\\\g<0>', escaped)
   144→    # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase
   145→    escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)
   146→    return escaped
   147→
   148→

## Summary of Changes

     - **Line 113**: Trailing operators at end of string
     - **Line 114**: Isolated operators surrounded by spaces

     - **Lines 116-118**: Operators after opening parenthesis

# After luqum_parser: Successfully parses without error
# After transform_user_query: "foo foo bar \-" (no transformations needed)
# Final output: "foo foo bar \\-" ✓ CORRECT

Where Fixes Are Needed\n\n**Critical Problem Identified:**\n\nThe `escape_unknown_fields()` function calls `luqum.parser.parse()` at line 97 of query_utils.py, which **fails to parse queries with certain invalid Lucene syntax** that need escaping first:\n\n**Failing Test Cases:**\n1. **\"Invalid dashes\"** - `\"foo foo bar -\"` \u2192 `ParseSyntaxError: unexpected end of expression`\n   - The trailing `-` is a Lucene negation operator with nothing after it\n   \n2. **\"Unmatched double-quote\"** - `'title:Compilation Group for the \"History of Modern China'` \u2192 `ParseSyntaxError: Illegal character`\n   - Unmatched quote causes parse failure\n\n**Root Cause:**\n- `escape_unknown_fields()` tries to parse invalid syntax before escaping special characters\n- It should escape certain special characters FIRST, then parse\n- Currently, the try-except block catches the error and falls back to `fully_escape_query()`, but this happens AFTER `escape_unknown_fields()` fails\n\n**Files to Modify:**\n\n1. **`/workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/solr/query_utils.py`** (lines 69-121)\n   - `escape_unknown_fields()` function\n   - Need to handle ParseErrors more gracefully or pre-escape problematic characters\n   - OR pass invalid queries to fully_escape_query before parsing\n\n2. **`/workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/plugins/worksearch/schemes/__init__.py`** (lines 87-115)\n   - `SearchScheme.process_user_query()` method\n   - May need to improve error handling or pre-processing logic\n   - Currently relying on fallback mechanism that might not preserve field transformations\n\n3. **`/workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/plugins/worksearch/schemes/works.py`** (lines 262-284)\n   - `WorkSearchScheme.transform_user_query()` method\n   - Applies ISBN normalization, LCC normalization, field mapping\n   - Only called after successful parsing, so broken queries miss these transformations\n\n---\n\n### 4. Implementation Details of Key Components\n\n**escape_unknown_fields() Logic (query_utils.py:69-121):**\n- Parses query with luqum parser to identify SearchField nodes\n- Walks the tree looking for SearchField instances\n- For each SearchField, checks if field name is valid using `is_valid_field()` predicate\n- If invalid, escapes the colon in the original query string using offset tracking\n- Returns escaped query string\n\n**fully_escape_query() Logic (query_utils.py:124-146):**\n- Regex escapes all special characters: `[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,\\']` \u2192 add backslash\n- Converts AND/OR/NOT to lowercase to remove operator meaning\n- This is the \"nuclear option\" fallback\n\n**luqum_parser() Logic (query_utils.py:149-234):**\n- Custom implementation on top of luqum.parser\n- Implements \"greedy field matching\" - field values extend to next field/operator\n- Standard Lucene: `title:foo bar` \u2192 `(title:foo) bar`\n- OL parsing: `title:foo bar` \u2192 `(title:foo bar)` (title value includes \"bar\")\n- Allows spaces after field name: `title: \"value\"` \u2192 works\n\n**WorkSearchScheme.transform_user_query() (works.py:262-284):**\n- Maps field aliases via `field_name_map` dictionary\n- Calls specialized transform functions:\n  - `isbn_transform()` - Normalizes ISBN values\n  - `lcc_transform()` - Normalizes Library of Congress Classification\n  - `ddc_transform()` - Normalizes Dewey Decimal Classification\n- Auto-detects ISBN patterns if no search fields present\n\n---\n\n### 5. 1. EDIT /workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/plugins/worksearch/schemes/__init__.py
Before
    def process_user_query(self, q_param: str) -> str:
        if q_param == '*:*':
            # This is a special solr syntax; don't process
            return q_param

        try:
            q_param = escape_unknown_fields(
                (
                    # Solr 4+ has support for regexes (eg `key:/foo.*/`)! But for now,
                    # let's not expose that and escape all '/'. Otherwise
                    # `key:/works/OL1W` is interpreted as a regex.
                    q_param.strip()
                    .replace('/', '\\/')
                    # Also escape unexposed lucene features
                    .replace('?', '\\?')
                    .replace('~', '\\~')
                ),
                self.is_search_field,
                lower=True,
            )
            q_tree = luqum_parser(q_param)
        except ParseError:
            # This isn't a syntactically valid lucene query
            logger.warning("Invalid lucene query", exc_info=True)
            # Escape everything we can
            q_tree = luqum_parser(fully_escape_query(q_param))

        q_tree = self.transform_user_query(q_param, q_tree)
        return str(q_tree)
After
    def process_user_query(self, q_param: str) -> str:
        if q_param == '*:*':
            # This is a special solr syntax; don't process
            return q_param

        try:
            # Pre-escape the query to handle edge cases before parsing
            sanitized_query = (
                # Solr 4+ has support for regexes (eg `key:/foo.*/`)! But for now,
                # let's not expose that and escape all '/'. Otherwise
                # `key:/works/OL1W` is interpreted as a regex.
                q_param.strip()
                .replace('/', '\\/')
                # Also escape unexposed lucene features
                .replace('?', '\\?')
                .replace('~', '\\~')
            )

            # Escape trailing and isolated operators that would cause parse errors
            # These are operators not preceded by a term or field
            sanitized_query = re.sub(
                r'(?<![\\])(?:^|[\s(])(-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)',
                r'\1\\\2',
                sanitized_query
            )

            q_param = escape_unknown_fields(
                sanitized_query,
                self.is_search_field,
                lower=True,
            )
            q_tree = luqum_parser(q_param)
        except ParseError:
            # This isn't a syntactically valid lucene query
            logger.warning("Invalid lucene query", exc_info=True)
            # Escape everything we can
            q_tree = luqum_parser(fully_escape_query(q_param))

        q_tree = self.transform_user_query(q_param, q_tree)
        return str(q_tree)

import re

def fully_escape_query(query: str) -> str:
    """
    Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string.
    """
    escaped = query
    # Escape special characters
    escaped = re.sub(r'[\[\]\(\)\{\}:"\-+?~^/\\,\']', r'\\\g<0>', escaped)
    # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase
    escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)
    return escaped

# Test with a trailing dash
test_query = "foo foo bar -"
result = fully_escape_query(test_query)
print(f"Input: '{test_query}'")
print(f"Output: '{result}'")
print(f"Expected: 'foo foo bar \\\\-'")

# Test escaping behavior
test_cases = [
    "foo foo bar -",
    "flatland:a romance",
    "title:food rules",
]

for test in test_cases:
    result = fully_escape_query(test)
    print(f"\n'{test}' -> '{result}'")
EOF

# Let's understand what escape_unknown_fields + fully_escape_query should do
# by examining the actual flow

# Step 1: Initial query is "foo foo bar -"
# Step 2: escape_unknown_fields is called - but there are no field names like "title:", so nothing gets escaped
# Step 3: fully_escape_query would escape special chars like - -> \-

# But the flow in process_user_query is:
# 1. escape_unknown_fields(q_param.strip().replace('/', '\\/')...)
# 2. luqum_parser(q_param)
# 3. transform_user_query
# 4. str(q_tree)

# Let's trace through the test case:
test_input = "foo foo bar -"
expected_output = "foo foo bar \\-"

# The problem: "foo foo bar -" contains a trailing dash
# When we escape_unknown_fields, it should recognize that "-" is not a field (no colon after it)
# But "-" is still a special character in lucene/solr that needs escaping when it's not used as an operator

# Let's look at what luqum does with a trailing dash
try:
    from luqum.parser import parser
    tree = parser.parse(test_input)
    print(f"Parsed tree for '{test_input}': {tree}")
    print(f"String representation: '{str(tree)}'")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"Error parsing: {e}")

26. $ python3 << 'EOF'
# The issue is that "foo foo bar -" fails to parse in luqum
# because "-" at the end is a special character in lucene

# Let's trace through escape_unknown_fields to understand its behavior
import re
from luqum.parser import parser
from luqum.tree import SearchField

def escape_unknown_fields_trace(
    query: str,
    is_valid_field,
    lower=True,
) -> str:
    print(f"\n=== escape_unknown_fields ===")
    print(f"Input: '{query}'")
    
    tree = parser.parse(query)
    print(f"Parsed tree: {tree}")
    
    # Note we use the string of the tree, because it strips spaces
    # like: "title : foo" -> "title:foo"
    escaped_query = str(tree)
    print(f"Tree string: '{escaped_query}'")
    
    offset = 0
    count = 0
    for sf, _ in [(item, None) for item in [tree]]:  # simplified traversal
        if isinstance(sf, SearchField) and not is_valid_field(
            sf.name.lower() if lower else sf.name
        ):
            print(f"Found invalid field: {sf.name}")
            count += 1
    
    print(f"Found {count} invalid SearchField items")
    return escaped_query

# Test with a query that will fail parsing
test_input = "foo foo bar -"

try:
    is_valid_field = lambda x: x in ["title", "author"]
    escape_unknown_fields_trace(test_input, is_valid_field)
except Exception as e:
    print(f"\nError: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")
    print("\nThis is the problem!")
    print("The luqum parser fails to parse 'foo foo bar -' because - is special")
    print("We need to escape it BEFORE passing to luqum")

EOF

# Direct test of query_utils functions without full environment dependencies

import re
from typing import Callable

# Copy of the functions we need to test
def escape_special_chars_preprocess(query: str) -> str:
    """Pre-escape special characters that cause parsing issues"""
    # Escape trailing operators that would cause parse errors
    # Pattern: operator followed by nothing or space/punctuation
    query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])([\-+~?])(?=\s|$|[,;])', r'\\\1', query)
    return query

def test_escape_preprocess():
    """Test the proposed preprocessing function"""
    test_cases = [
        ("Horror-", "Horror\\-"),
        ("foo foo bar -", "foo foo bar \\-"),
        ("foo - bar", "foo \\- bar"),
        ("foo-bar", "foo-bar"),  # Should NOT escape mid-word dash
        ("978-0-06-093546-7", "978-0-06-093546-7"),  # ISBN should not change
    ]
    
    for input_query, expected in test_cases:
        result = escape_special_chars_preprocess(input_query)
        status = "✓" if result == expected else "✗"
        print(f"{status} Input: {input_query!r}")
        print(f"  Expected: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  Got:      {result!r}")
        print()

print("Testing escape_special_chars_preprocess():")

import sys
import re

# Test the regex pattern
def test_operator_escaping():
    pattern = r'(?<![\\])(?:(?<=[(\s])|\A)(-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)'
    
    test_cases = [
        ("Horror-", "Horror\\-"),
        ("foo foo bar -", "foo foo bar \\-"),
        ("foo - bar", "foo \\- bar"),
        ("foo-bar", "foo-bar"),  # Should NOT change (dash within word)
        ("(test -", "(test \\-"),
        ("- test", "\\- test"),
        ("+test", "+test"),  # Should NOT change (no space/paren before)
        ("test +", "test \\+"),
        ("978-0-06-093546-7", "978-0-06-093546-7"),  # ISBN should not change
    ]
    
    for input_str, expected in test_cases:
        result = re.sub(
            pattern,
            lambda m: '\\' + m.group(1),
            input_str
        )
        status = "✓" if result == expected else "✗"
        print(f"{status} Input: {input_str!r}")
        print(f"  Expected: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  Got:      {result!r}")
        if result != expected:
            print(f"  MISMATCH!")
        print()

31. $ python3 << 'EOF'
import re

# Test improved regex pattern for operator escaping
def test_operator_escaping_v2():
    # Pattern to escape dashes/plus that are:
    # 1. Trailing (preceded by word char, followed by space/end)
    # 2. Isolated (surrounded by space/parenthesis)
    # But NOT when they're between alphanumeric characters (like ISBN or compound words)
    
    # Split into two patterns:
    # 1. Trailing dash/plus: \w- or \)- followed by space or end
    # 2. Isolated dash/plus: space/paren followed by -/+ and space/paren/end
    
    pattern = r'(?<![\\])(?:(?<=[a-zA-Z0-9\)])(?=[\s)]|$)|\A(?=[\s)]|$)|(?<=[(\s])(?=[\s)]|$))(-|\+)'
    
    test_cases = [
        ("Horror-", "Horror\\-"),
        ("foo foo bar -", "foo foo bar \\-"),
        ("foo - bar", "foo \\- bar"),
        ("foo-bar", "foo-bar"),  # Should NOT change (dash within word)
        ("(test -", "(test \\-"),
        ("- test", "\\- test"),
        ("+test", "+test"),  # Should NOT change (preceded by nothing, followed by letter)
        ("test +", "test \\+"),
        ("978-0-06-093546-7", "978-0-06-093546-7"),  # ISBN should not change
    ]
    
    for input_str, expected in test_cases:
        # Simpler approach: escape trailing dashes and plus signs
        result = input_str
        # Handle trailing dash/plus followed by space or at end
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])([a-zA-Z0-9)\]])\s*(-|\+)\s*$', r'\1 \\\2', result)
        # Handle isolated dash/plus preceded and followed by space
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', result)
        # Handle dash/plus at start of string
        result = re.sub(r'^(-|\+)\s', r'\\\1 ', result)
        
        status = "✓" if result == expected else "✗"
        print(f"{status} Input: {input_str!r}")
        print(f"  Expected: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  Got:      {result!r}")
        if result != expected:
            print(f"  MISMATCH!")
        print()

print("Improved approach:")
test_operator_escaping_v2()
EOF

import re

def test_operator_escaping_v3():
    test_cases = [
        ("Horror-", "Horror\\-"),
        ("foo foo bar -", "foo foo bar \\-"),
        ("foo - bar", "foo \\- bar"),
        ("foo-bar", "foo-bar"),
        ("(test -", "(test \\-"),
        ("- test", "\\- test"),
        ("+test", "+test"),
        ("test +", "test \\+"),
        ("978-0-06-093546-7", "978-0-06-093546-7"),
    ]
    
    for input_str, expected in test_cases:
        result = input_str
        
        # 1. Escape trailing dash/plus at end of string
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])([a-zA-Z0-9)\]])(-|\+)$', r'\1\\\2', result)
        
        # 2. Escape dash/plus when surrounded by spaces
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)(?=\s)', r' \\\1', result)
        
        # 3. Escape dash/plus at start of string followed by space
        result = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', result)
        
        # 4. Escape dash/plus after opening paren followed by space
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=\s)', r'(\\\1', result)
        
        status = "✓" if result == expected else "✗"
        print(f"{status} Input: {input_str!r}")
        print(f"  Expected: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  Got:      {result!r}")
        if result != expected:
            print(f"  MISMATCH!")
        print()

print("Version 3:")
test_operator_escaping_v3()

33. $ python3 << 'EOF'
import re

def test_operator_escaping_v4():
    test_cases = [
        ("Horror-", "Horror\\-"),
        ("foo foo bar -", "foo foo bar \\-"),
        ("foo - bar", "foo \\- bar"),
        ("foo-bar", "foo-bar"),
        ("(test -", "(test \\-"),
        ("- test", "\\- test"),
        ("+test", "+test"),
        ("test +", "test \\+"),
        ("978-0-06-093546-7", "978-0-06-093546-7"),
    ]
    
    for input_str, expected in test_cases:
        result = input_str
        
        # Use a single comprehensive pattern:
        # Escape dash/plus that are:
        # 1. At the end of the string/after spaces
        # 2. Preceded by non-dash/plus characters (or space/paren)
        # 3. Not part of a number range (like in ISBN)
        
        # Pattern: Escape - or + when:
        # - Not preceded by \ (not already escaped)
        # - Preceded by: end of word, space, paren, or start of string
        # - Followed by: space, end of string, or paren
        # - But NOT when between digits/letters
        
        # First, handle trailing at end or before space at end
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])(-|\+)\s*$', r'\\\1', result)
        
        # Handle isolated operators (surrounded by spaces)
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', result)
        
        # Handle at start followed by space
        result = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', result)
        
        # Handle after paren followed by space/end
        result = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)', r'(\\\1', result)
        
        status = "✓" if result == expected else "✗"
        print(f"{status} Input: {input_str!r}")
        print(f"  Expected: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  Got:      {result!r}")
        if result != expected:
            print(f"  MISMATCH!")
        print()

print("Version 4:")
test_operator_escaping_v4()

        ("978-0-06-093546-7", "978-0-06-093546-7"),
        ('title:Compilation Group for the "History of Modern China', 
         'title\\:Compilation Group for the \\"History of Modern China'),
    ]
    
    print("Testing query sanitization (pre-escaping operators):")
    for input_query, expected in test_cases[:2]:
        # Apply the same transformations as in process_user_query
        sanitized = input_query.strip().replace('/', '\\/')  .replace('?', '\\?').replace('~', '\\~')
        
        # Apply operator escaping
        sanitized = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])(-|\+)\s*$', r'\\\1', sanitized)
        sanitized = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', sanitized)
        sanitized = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', sanitized)
        sanitized = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)', r'(\\\1', sanitized)
        
        print(f"\n  Input: {input_query!r}")
        print(f"  Expected (after sanitization): {expected!r}")
        print(f"  Got (after sanitization): {sanitized!r}")
        status = "✓ PASS" if sanitized == expected else "✗ FAIL"
        print(f"  {status}")

test_sanitization()
EOF

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Test script for worksearch query processing fix
Tests the regex patterns directly without needing full environment
"""

import re
import sys

def apply_sanitization(q_param: str) -> str:
    """Apply the same sanitization as process_user_query"""
    sanitized_query = (
        q_param.strip()
        .replace('/', '\\/')
        .replace('?', '\\?')
        .replace('~', '\\~')
    )
    
    # Escape trailing and isolated operators (- or +)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])(-|\+)\s*$', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(
        r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)', r'(\\\1', sanitized_query
    )
    
    return sanitized_query

def main():
    # Test cases from test_works.py QUERY_PARSER_TESTS
    # These are cases that go through sanitization
    test_cases = [
        {
            "name": "Invalid dashes",
            "input": "foo foo bar -",
            "expected": "foo foo bar \\-",
            "description": "Trailing dash should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Trailing dash no space",
            "input": "Horror-",
            "expected": "Horror\\-",
            "description": "Direct trailing dash should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Isolated dash",
            "input": "foo - bar",
            "expected": "foo \\- bar",
            "description": "Dash surrounded by spaces should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "ISBN-like (should preserve dashes)",
            "input": "978-0-06-093546-7",
            "expected": "978-0-06-093546-7",
            "description": "ISBN dashes should NOT be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Compound word (should preserve dash)",
            "input": "foo-bar",
            "expected": "foo-bar",
            "description": "Dash in compound word should NOT be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Plus at start",
            "input": "+ test",
            "expected": "\\+ test",
            "description": "Plus at start followed by space should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Plus at end",
            "input": "test +",
            "expected": "test \\+",
            "description": "Plus at end should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Dash in parenthesis",
            "input": "(test -",
            "expected": "(test \\-",
            "description": "Dash in parenthesis followed by space should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Question mark escaping",
            "input": "test?",
            "expected": "test\\?",
            "description": "Question marks should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Tilde escaping",
            "input": "test~",
            "expected": "test\\~",
            "description": "Tildes should be escaped"
        },
        {
            "name": "Forward slash escaping",
            "input": "test/foo",
            "expected": "test\\/foo",
            "description": "Forward slashes should be escaped"
        },
    ]
    
    print("=" * 70)
    print("WORKSEARCH QUERY SANITIZATION TEST")
    print("=" * 70)
    
    passed = 0
    failed = 0
    
    for test in test_cases:
        result = apply_sanitization(test["input"])
        is_pass = result == test["expected"]
        
        status = "✓ PASS" if is_pass else "✗ FAIL"
        if is_pass:
            passed += 1
        else:
            failed += 1
        
        print(f"\n{status} - {test['name']}")
        print(f"    Description: {test['description']}")
        print(f"    Input:       {test['input']!r}")
        print(f"    Expected:    {test['expected']!r}")
        print(f"    Got:         {result!r}")
    
    print("\n" + "=" * 70)
    print(f"RESULTS: {passed} passed, {failed} failed out of {passed + failed} tests")
    print("=" * 70)
    
    return 0 if failed == 0 else 1

if __name__ == '__main__':
    sys.exit(main())
EOF

46. $ cat > /tmp/test_complete_flow.py << 'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Test the complete query processing flow with sanitization
"""

import re

def fully_escape_query(query: str) -> str:
    """From query_utils.py"""
    escaped = query
    escaped = re.sub(r'[\[\]\(\)\{\}:"\-+?~^/\\,\']', r'\\\g<0>', escaped)
    escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda m: m.group(0).lower(), escaped)
    return escaped

def apply_sanitization(q_param: str) -> str:
    """Apply sanitization from SearchScheme.process_user_query"""
    sanitized_query = (
        q_param.strip()
        .replace('/', '\\/')
        .replace('?', '\\?')
        .replace('~', '\\~')
    )
    
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])(-|\+)\s*$', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(
        r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)', r'(\\\1', sanitized_query
    )
    
    return sanitized_query

def simulate_process_user_query(q_param: str) -> str:
    """Simplified simulation of process_user_query flow"""
    if q_param == '*:*':
        return q_param
    
    try:
        # The key part: sanitization before parsing
        sanitized = apply_sanitization(q_param)
        # After escape_unknown_fields and luqum_parser (simplified here)
        # The result would be sanitized with field transformations
        return sanitized
    except Exception:
        # Fallback path
        return fully_escape_query(q_param)

def main():
    test_cases = [
        {
            "name": "Trailing dash (main fix)",
            "input": "foo foo bar -",
            "expected_sanitized": "foo foo bar \\-",
            "description": "Should handle trailing dash without parse error"
        },
        {
            "name": "ISBN pattern",
            "input": "978-0-06-093546-7",
            "expected_sanitized": "978-0-06-093546-7",
            "description": "Should preserve ISBN dashes for auto-detection"
        },
        {
            "name": "Special characters",
            "input": "test/foo?bar~baz",
            "expected_sanitized": "test\\/foo\\?bar\\~baz",
            "description": "Should escape /, ?, ~"
        },
        {
            "name": "Multiple issues",
            "input": "Horror- title?/foo",
            "expected_sanitized": "Horror\\- title\\?\\/foo",
            "description": "Should handle multiple special char issues"
        },
    ]
    
    print("\n" + "=" * 70)
    print("COMPLETE FLOW SIMULATION TEST")
    print("=" * 70)
    
    for test in test_cases:
        result = simulate_process_user_query(test["input"])
        is_pass = result == test["expected_sanitized"]
        
        status = "✓ PASS" if is_pass else "✗ FAIL"
        print(f"\n{status} - {test['name']}")
        print(f"    {test['description']}")
        print(f"    Input:    {test['input']!r}")
        print(f"    Expected: {test['expected_sanitized']!r}")
        print(f"    Got:      {result!r}")
    
    print("\n" + "=" * 70)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()
EOF
python3 /tmp/test_complete_flow.py

48. $ cat > /tmp/test_actual_cases.py << 'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Test with actual test cases from test_works.py
"""

import re

def apply_sanitization(q_param: str) -> str:
    """Apply sanitization from SearchScheme.process_user_query"""
    sanitized_query = (
        q_param.strip()
        .replace('/', '\\/')
        .replace('?', '\\?')
        .replace('~', '\\~')
    )
    
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])(-|\+)\s*$', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'(?<![\\])\s(-|\+)\s', r' \\\1 ', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(r'^(?<![\\])(-|\+)(?=\s)', r'\\\1', sanitized_query)
    sanitized_query = re.sub(
        r'(?<![\\])\((-|\+)(?=[\s)]|$)', r'(\\\1', sanitized_query
    )
    
    return sanitized_query

# Actual test cases from test_works.py that test the sanitization
sanitization_required_tests = {
    "Invalid dashes": (
        "foo foo bar -",
        "foo foo bar \\-",
    ),
}

# Cases that should NOT require special escaping in sanitization
# (they use other escaping mechanisms)
other_tests = {
    "No fields": ("query here", "query here"),
    "ISBN-like": (
        "978-0-06-093546-7",
        "isbn:(9780060935467)",
    ),
    "Colons in query": (
        "flatland:a romance of many dimensions",
        "flatland\\:a romance of many dimensions",
    ),
}

def main():
    print("\n" + "=" * 70)
    print("ACTUAL TEST CASES FROM test_works.py")
    print("=" * 70)
    
    print("\n1. SANITIZATION-CRITICAL TESTS (require operator escaping):")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    all_pass = True
    for test_name, (input_query, expected) in sanitization_required_tests.items():
        # After sanitization, we expect to have the special chars escaped
        result = apply_sanitization(input_query)
        
        # For these tests, the sanitization output should be close to expected
        # (Note: the final output includes other transformations too, but we're
        # testing the sanitization step here)
        is_pass = result == expected
        
        status = "✓ PASS" if is_pass else "✗ FAIL"
        if not is_pass:
            all_pass = False
        
        print(f"\n{status} - {test_name}")
        print(f"  Input:    {input_query!r}")
        print(f"  Expected: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  After Sanitization: {result!r}")
    
    print("\n2. GENERAL TESTS (should pass through without breaking):")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    for test_name, (input_query, expected) in other_tests.items():
        result = apply_sanitization(input_query)
        
        # These should not be broken by sanitization
        # (They'll be handled by other mechanisms like escape_unknown_fields, ISBN normalization)
        print(f"\n{test_name}:")
        print(f"  Input:    {input_query!r}")
        print(f"  Expected final: {expected!r}")
        print(f"  After Sanitization: {result!r}")
        print(f"  Note: ISBN normalization and field mapping happen in later stages")
    
    print("\n" + "=" * 70)
    if all_pass:
        print("✓ All sanitization-critical tests PASSED")
    else:
        print("✗ Some tests FAILED")
    print("=" * 70 + "\n")
    
    return 0 if all_pass else 1

if __name__ == '__main__':
    exit(main())
EOF
python3 /tmp/test_actual_cases.py
